- echo whispers
- loss of motor control
- rage episodes

### **5.3. Spiritual Costs**

- spirit hostility
- shrine rejection
- loss of spirit contract trust
- Echo-layer sickness
- nightmares with teeth

### **5.4. World Costs**

This is the most important part:

Forbidden arts **damage the world**.

Examples:

- creating corrupted scars
- destabilizing anomaly cracks
- corrupting soil/trees
- wildlife mutation
- NPC fear and panic
- increased collapse instability

Forbidden techniques are **not private acts**.  
They ripple outward.

The player is responsible.

---

# **6. Forbidden Glyph Sequences (Corrupted Combo Evolution)**

Corrupted glyph sequences differ from normal combos:

### They are:

- longer
- unstable
- harder to memorize
- painful to perform
- violent to chakra coils
- more chaotic in output
- influenced by corruption density
- evolving across world seeds

A normal combo might be 5â€“12 signs.  
High-tier combos might hit 15â€“20.

Corrupted sequences can reach **30+** signs â€”  
borderline rituals expressed through hand movement.

### Effects include:

- mutated elemental techniques
- shadow propagation
- corruption-fueled blasts
- dark doubles
- partial etherealization
- echo flicker illusions
- blood-reactive seals
- corruption vines, tendrils

These are extremely deadly to user and enemy alike.

---

# **7. Residue Overgrowth â€” World-Affecting Waves (Choice: C)**

This is where forbidden arts become **world-design systems**.

Residue overgrowth occurs when:

- corruption accumulates
- forbidden arts are over-used
- instability rises
- anomalies destabilize
- spirits retreat
- collapse states begin

Residue overgrowth spreads like:

- corrupted vines
- blackened soil
- glowing spore fields
- corrupted fog
- biome mutation
- sick wildlife
- cracked earth

### Overgrowth powers:

- corruption creatures
- dark spirits
- mutated wildlife
- corrupted NPCs
- aberration nests

### World consequences:

- region lockdown
- NPC migration
- spirits avoid area
- political instability
- clan blame
- anomalies intensify
- collapse seeds ignite

Forbidden arts are **one of the major triggers** of collapse states (C6).

---

# **8. Player Accessibility â€œYes, alwaysâ€ (Choice: A)**

This means:

- Spirit contracts (C3) are rare and dependent on world conditions.
- **Forbidden arts (C4) are always accessible** because corruption is always present.

Any player can:

- find corruption
- use forbidden glyphs
- mutate
- overclock chakra
- become an aberration

But few survive.

Forbidden arts are the **universal dark path**:

- a constant temptation
- an always-present shortcut
- the dangerous â€œeasyâ€ option

This mirrors:

- Curse Mark
- Dark senjutsu
- Unstable tailed-beast states

It gives the player an escape:  
â€œEven if the world has no great spirits, I can still become powerful.â€

At enormous cost.

---

# **9. World Reaction to Forbidden Arts**

NPCs respond strongly to corruption usage:

### **Civilized factions:**

- fear
- arrest
- exile
- clinical observation
- political exploitation

### **Clans:**

- some ban forbidden arts
- some weaponize them
- some conduct research
- some execute users

### **Outlaw groups:**

- revere corruption
- recruit aberrants
- use corrupted zones as hideouts

### **Spirits:**

- become hostile
- refuse contracts
- warn others
- lose trust

### **Corruption Entities:**

- grow stronger near users
- spawn more creatures
- track corrupted chakra signatures

Forbidden arts shape reputation (B28).

---

# **10. Integration with C1**

Forbidden arts **flirt** with mythic evolution but DO NOT cause it.

Differences:

- Corrupted aberrations are unstable; mythic evolution is stable transcendence.
- Corruption warps the body; mythic evolution reshapes reality.
- Forbidden arts destroy world stability; mythic evolution can either degrade or elevate it.
- Forbidden arts isolate you from spirits; mythic evolution attracts their attention.
- Forbidden arts are always available; mythic evolution is rare and emergent.

This distinction preserves the C-series hierarchy.

---

# **C4 â€” Final Summary**

Forbidden Arts in Sigilborne are:

- **controllable corruption**
- **voluntary power escalation**
- **extremely dangerous**
- **highly mutagenic**
- **always accessible**

Aberrations are:

- humanoid but monstrous
- path-dependent
- influenced by world seed
- unique per player experience

Forbidden Arts are Sigilborne's way of saying:

> Power is always available.  
> But at a price the world will never forget.

# **1. What Collapse Actually Means (Philosophical Definition)**

Collapse is the **failure of systems** that keep the world stable:

- ecological cycles
- spiritual resonance
- anomaly containment
- corruption boundaries
- political equilibrium
- titan territories
- clan hierarchies
- mirror-realms (Echo)
- shrine networks
- leyline flows

A collapse is not one event.  
Itâ€™s the **avalanche** that happens once the mountain finally gives way.

Your choice: **Collapse triggered by accumulated instability (B).**

# **2. Collapse Frequency â€” 1â€“3 Per World (Choice: B)**

Most worlds experience:

- **0 major collapses** (rare, stable seeds)
- **1 collapse** (common)

- **3 collapses** (very unstable worlds, collapse-heavy seeds)

These collapses:

- do NOT always reach catastrophic levels
- can happen at different times
- may be small or massive
- depend on worldâ€™s dynamic instability index (from B31)

> Only a Sigilborne can survive the instability of worlds long enough to bind glyphs and shape destiny.

The title is not bestowed.  
It is inherent.

Not rare.  
Not mythical.  
Not divine.

Simply:  
**Those who can perceive and survive the Echoâ€™s shifting geometry.**

---

# **11. Final Canon Statement**

Sigilborne has no one true ending.  
No one true world.  
No absolute canon.

Instead:

- Each world you generate is its own history.
- Each life you live is its own story.
- Each collapse is its own tragedy.
- Each titan is its own myth.
- Each spirit is its own dream.
- Each Echo is its own secret.
- Each glyph is its own meaning.

Sigilborneâ€™s real canon is:  
**The infinite multiverse of stories you create.**

The Echo remembers.  
The worlds evolve.  
You begin again.

# Technical Design Document (TDD)
# TDD 00: Technical Overview & Philosophy

## 1. The "Brain & Body" Architecture
Sigilborne utilizes a hybrid **Godot 4.5 + C#** architecture to balance high-performance simulation with rapid visual iteration.

### **The Brain (C#)**
*   **Role**: The "Server" logic running locally.
*   **Responsibility**: Heavy simulation, data management, AI decision-making, procedural generation, and global state.
*   **Constraint**: **HEADLESS**. The Brain should generally *not* know about Godot Nodes (`Node3D`, `Sprite2D`, etc.) unless absolutely necessary for physics. It operates on pure data (Structs, Classes).
*   **Performance**: Uses `structs` and `Span<T>` to minimize Garbage Collection (GC) pressure.

### **The Body (GDScript)**
*   **Role**: The "Client" presentation layer.
*   **Responsibility**: Rendering, Audio, Input handling, UI, Animations, and Particle effects.
*   **Constraint**: **REACTIVE**. The Body does not calculate *results*; it visualizes the *state* provided by the Brain.
*   **Performance**: Optimized for frame-rate and visual smoothness.

---

## 2. Directory Structure
The project follows a strict separation of concerns in the file system.

```text
res://
â”œâ”€â”€ _Brain/                 # C# Source Code (The Simulation)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Core/               # Main Loop, Event Bus, Time
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Systems/            # Magic, Combat, Ecology, Economy
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Data/               # Static Data (Items, Spells)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Utils/              # Math, Extensions
â”œâ”€â”€ _Body/                  # Godot Assets (The Visuals)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Scenes/             # .tscn files
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Scripts/            # .gd files (Visual logic only)
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Art/                # Sprites, Textures, Shaders
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Audio/              # Banks, Streams
â”œâ”€â”€ _Shared/                # Resources used by both (if any)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ Config/             # Settings, Constants
â””â”€â”€ Main.tscn               # Entry Point
```

---

## 3. Coding Standards

### **C# (The Brain)**
*   **Naming**: PascalCase for classes/methods (`CalculateDamage`), camelCase for locals (`currentHealth`).
*   **Data**: Prefer `readonly struct` for data passing.
*   **Collections**: Use `List<T>` or `Dictionary<TKey, TValue>` for lookups. Avoid LINQ in hot paths (Update loops).

### **GDScript (The Body)**
*   **Naming**: snake_case for variables/functions (`play_animation`), PascalCase for Classes (`PlayerController`).
*   **Typing**: **ALWAYS** use static typing (`var health: float = 100.0`).
*   **Signal**: Use `signal_name.emit()` syntax.

---

## 4. The TDD Roadmap
This Technical Design Document is split into the following chapters:

1.  **Architecture & Core Engine**: The spine of the project.
2.  **Magic & Casting**: The complex spell system.
3.  **Biological Simulation**: Health, weather, and survival.
4.  **Combat & Equipment**: Damage, hitboxes, and inventory.
5.  **AI & Ecology**: NPC behavior and world simulation.
6.  **Society & Economy**: Factions, trade, and social graphs.
7.  **Progression & Meta**: Quests, save systems, and lore.
8.  **World Gen**: Procedural terrain and streaming.
9.  **Advanced World**: Rituals and catastrophes.
10. **Audio & VFX**: Feedback pipelines.
# TDD 01: Architecture & Core Engine

## 1. High-Level Architecture
The core engine acts as the bridge between the **Brain (C#)** and the **Body (GDScript)**. It is responsible for initializing the game, managing the main loop, and ensuring thread-safe communication between the simulation and the visuals.

### **The "Tick" vs. "Frame"**
*   **Simulation Tick (Brain)**: Fixed timestep (e.g., 20Hz or 0.05s). Deterministic. Updates the world state.
*   **Render Frame (Body)**: Variable timestep (Monitor Refresh Rate). Interpolates between simulation states for smooth visuals.

---

## 2. Core Components

### **2.1 GameManager (C#)**
The entry point for the C# logic. It is a `Node` attached to the root of the scene but serves only as a bootstrapper.

```csharp
// _Brain/Core/GameManager.cs
public partial class GameManager : Node
{
    public static GameManager Instance { get; private set; }
    
    // Systems
    public TimeSystem Time { get; private set; }
    public EventBus Events { get; private set; }
    public WorldSimulation World { get; private set; }

    public override void _Ready()
    {
        Instance = this;
        InitializeSystems();
    }

    public override void _PhysicsProcess(double delta)
    {
        // The Heartbeat of the Brain
        World.Tick(delta);
    }
}
```

### **2.2 SceneLoader (GDScript)**
Manages the transition between high-level game states (MainMenu, Loading, Gameplay).

```gdscript
# _Body/Scripts/Core/SceneLoader.gd
class_name SceneLoader extends Node

signal scene_loaded

func load_level(level_id: String) -> void:
    # Show Loading Screen
    # Request World Gen from Brain
    # Wait for "Ready" signal
    # Fade In
    pass
```

---

## 3. The Interop Layer (API)
Communication between C# and GDScript must be strict to prevent spaghetti code.

### **3.1 C# to GDScript (Signals)**
The Brain does not call functions on the Body directly. It emits **Signals**.
*   **Pattern**: `GameEvents.OnPlayerHealthChanged?.Invoke(newHealth);`
*   **GDScript Listener**: `GameEvents.connect("player_health_changed", _on_health_changed)`

### 3.3 The EventBus Contract
To prevent "Event Spaghetti", we enforce a strict contract.
*   **Type**: C# `Action<T>` delegates (Synchronous).
*   **Threading**: Events emitted from the Brain run on the **Main Thread** (during the Sync Phase) to allow safe Godot API calls.
*   **Batching**: Events generated by Background Jobs are added to a `ConcurrentQueue` and flushed at the start of the next frame.
*   **Error Handling**: Listeners are wrapped in `try/catch` blocks to prevent one UI error from crashing the simulation.

### 3.4 Interpolation Strategy
Since the Brain runs at 20Hz (Tick) and the Body at 60Hz+ (Frame), we must interpolate.
*   **Buffer**: The Body stores the last 2 Ticks of data: `State_Previous` and `State_Current`.
*   **Alpha**: `alpha = (Time.time - LastTickTime) / TickDuration`.
*   **Logic**: `VisualPos = Lerp(State_Previous.Pos, State_Current.Pos, alpha)`.
*   **Rubberbanding**: If the visual position drifts > 2.0 units from the authoritative state, we snap it instantly.

---

## 4. Global State Management
State is strictly owned by the Brain. The Body never "owns" data, it only displays it.

| Data Type | Owner | Example |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Player Stats** | C# `StatSystem` | Health: 100, Mana: 50 |
| **Inventory** | C# `InventorySystem` | [Sword, Potion, Map] |
| **World Time** | C# `TimeSystem` | Day 4, 14:00 |
| **NPC Positions** | C# `EcologyManager` | {ID: 101, Pos: (40, 20)} |
| **Visual Position** | GDScript `Node2D` | `position = lerp(prev, next, alpha)` |

---

## 5. Debugging Tools
To manage the complexity of a simulation game, we need robust debugging tools.

### **5.1 The Debug Console (GDScript + C#)**
A Quake-style console (`~` key) to execute commands.
*   **Implementation**: A GDScript UI layer that parses text and calls `DebugCommandSystem.Execute(command)` in C#.
*   **Commands**:
    *   `/give [item_id] [amount]`
    *   `/time set [hour]`
    *   `/godmode`

### **5.2 State Inspector**
A runtime UI overlay that displays the raw data of the entity under the cursor.
*   **Function**: Raycasts from mouse -> finds Entity ID -> queries C# `EntityManager` -> displays struct data in a UI window.

---

## 6. Main Loop Execution Order
1.  **_Process (GDScript)**:
    *   Capture Input -> Send to C# Buffer.
    *   Interpolate Visuals (Movement, Animation).
    *   Update UI.
2.  **_PhysicsProcess (C#)**:
    *   **Phase 1**: Process Input Buffer.
    *   **Phase 2**: Run Simulation Systems (Physics, AI, Biology).
    *   **Phase 3**: Resolve Collisions/Events.
    *   **Phase 4**: Emit State Update Signals.
# TDD 02: Magic & Casting Mechanics

## 1. Overview
The Magic System is the core gameplay loop of Sigilborne. It relies on a fighting-game-style input system where players input sequences of "Glyphs" (Keys) to cast spells.

**GDD References**: B01 (Glyphs), B02 (Combos), B03 (Stability), B05 (Hotbar), C01 (Mythic), C04 (Forbidden).

---

## 2. The Input Pipeline (Brain)

### **2.1 InputBuffer (C#)**
A circular buffer that stores the last `N` inputs with precise timestamps.

```csharp
public struct InputFrame
{
    public GlyphType Glyph; // Enum: Fire, Water, Void, etc.
    public double Timestamp;
    public bool Consumed;
}

public class InputBuffer
{
    private InputFrame[] _buffer = new InputFrame[20];
    private int _head;
    
    public void Push(GlyphType glyph, double time) { ... }
    public ReadOnlySpan<InputFrame> GetRecent(double window) { ... }
}
```

### **2.2 Combo Resolver (Trie Structure)**
To detect spells efficiently, we use a **Prefix Tree (Trie)**.
*   **Structure**: Each node in the Trie represents a Glyph.
*   **Leaf Nodes**: Contain the `SpellID` of the completed spell.
*   **Algorithm**:
    1.  On every input, traverse the Trie from the root using the `InputBuffer`.
    2.  If a valid path is found within the `MaxComboDelay`, trigger the spell.
    3.  **Optimization**: Store the Trie as a flat array of structs for cache locality.

---

## 3. Spell Data Architecture

### **3.1 Spell Definition (Resource/ScriptableObject)**
Spells are defined as data, not code, to allow for thousands of variations (C01 Mythic Evolution).

```csharp
public class SpellDefinition
{
    public string ID; // "fireball_01"
    public GlyphType[] Sequence; // [Fire, Fire, Wind]
    public float BaseDamage;
    public float ManaCost;
    public float CastTime;
    
    // Components (ECS-lite)
    public ProjectileData Projectile; // Speed, Size, Pierce
    public AoEData Explosion; // Radius, Falloff
    public StatusEffectData[] Effects; // Burn, Stun
}
```

### **3.2 Mythic Evolution (C01)**
When a spell evolves, we do not create a new class. We mutate the `SpellDefinition` data or swap it for a "Mythic" variant.
*   **Data Driven**: `fireball_mythic` is just another entry in the database with `IsMythic = true` and exaggerated stats/VFX IDs.

---

## 4. Casting State Machine (C#)

The player's casting state is managed by a strict State Machine in the Brain.

1.  **Idle**: Waiting for input.
2.  **Channeling**: Input sequence started. Visuals: Glyphs appearing.
3.  **CastStart**: Sequence complete. Mana deducted.
4.  **Casting**: The "Active Frames". Projectile spawns or effect applies.
5.  **Recovery**: The "End Lag". Player cannot move/act.

```csharp
public enum CastState { Idle, Channeling, Casting, Recovery }

public void Update(double delta)
{
    switch (CurrentState)
    {
        case CastState.Channeling:
            if (Time.time - LastInputTime > ResetTime) Reset();
            break;
        case CastState.Casting:
            if (Timer >= CurrentSpell.CastTime) EnterRecovery();
            break;
    }
}
```

---

## 5. Visual Feedback (Body)

The Body listens for state changes to play the "Puppet Show".

### **5.1 Particle Manager**
*   **Signal**: `OnGlyphInput(GlyphType type)`
*   **Reaction**: Spawn a 2D GPU Particle system at the player's location. Color matches the element (Red=Fire).
*   **Optimization**: Use `GPUParticles2D` with a pre-allocated pool.

### **5.2 Animation Controller**
*   **Signal**: `OnCastStart(SpellID id)`
*   **Reaction**: Play the specific animation for that spell (e.g., "Two-Handed Slam" for Earth spells).

---

## 6. Stability & Chaos (B03, C04)

### **6.1 Stability Meter**
A float value (0.0 to 1.0) tracked in C#.
*   **Decay**: Regenerates slowly over time.
*   **Cost**: Every spell reduces stability.
*   **Threshold**: If Stability < 0, trigger **Chaos Event**.

### **6.2 Chaos Residue (C04)**
When casting "Forbidden" spells, `Residue` accumulates in the chunk.
*   **Implementation**: A `Dictionary<Vector2Int, float>` in the `WorldManager`.
*   **Effect**: If Residue > 100 in a chunk, spawn "Void Aberrations" (See TDD 05 AI).
# TDD 03: Biological & Environmental Simulation

## 1. Overview
This chapter details the "Survival" aspect of Sigilborne. The Brain simulates the biological needs of the player and NPCs, as well as the dynamic weather systems that affect them.

**GDD References**: B08 (Biology), B12 (Recovery), B14 (Survival), C04 (Residue).

---

## 2. The Biological Simulation (Brain)

### **2.1 The Bio-Tick**
Unlike combat, biological stats do not need to update every frame. We use a **Bio-Tick** (e.g., 1Hz or once per second) to save performance.

```csharp
public class BiologicalSim
{
    private const float TICK_RATE = 1.0f;
    private float _timer;

    public void Update(double delta)
    {
        _timer += (float)delta;
        if (_timer >= TICK_RATE)
        {
            ProcessTick();
            _timer = 0;
        }
    }
}
```

### **2.2 Core Stats (Struct)**
We use a `readonly struct` to pass state around safely.

```csharp
public struct BioState
{
    public float Health;
    public float MaxHealth;
    public float Stamina;
    public float Chakra;
    public float Hunger; // 0-100
    public float Thirst; // 0-100
    public float BodyTemp; // Celsius
}
```

### **2.3 Metabolism System**
Hunger and Thirst decay rates are dynamic, based on the `ActivityLevel`.

*   **Idle**: 1x Decay
*   **Running**: 2x Decay
*   **Combat**: 5x Decay
*   **Casting**: Consumes Chakra + Small Hunger spike.

**Formula**:
`Hunger -= BaseDecay * ActivityMultiplier * WeatherMultiplier`

---

## 3. Weather & Environment (Brain)

### **3.1 Weather State**
The `WeatherSystem` is a global singleton in the Brain.

```csharp
public enum WeatherType { Clear, Rain, Storm, Snow, Fog, AshFall }

public class WeatherSystem
{
    public WeatherType CurrentWeather;
    public Vector2 WindDirection;
    public float Temperature; // Ambient
    public float Humidity;
}
```

### **3.2 Environmental Pressure**
The environment directly impacts the `BioState`.
*   **Cold (Snow)**: Increases `Hunger` decay (burning calories to stay warm). Lowers `BodyTemp`.
*   **Hot (Desert)**: Increases `Thirst` decay.
*   **AshFall (C04)**: Increases `Chakra` instability.

---

## 4. Damage & Recovery (B12)

### **4.1 Damage Pipeline**
When an entity takes damage, it passes through a pipeline:
1.  **Raw Damage**: Incoming value.
2.  **Mitigation**: Armor reduction.
3.  **Application**: Subtract from Health.
4.  **Wound Generation**: Chance to create a `StatusEffect` (Bleed, Fracture).

### **4.2 Recovery Logic**
# TDD 04: Combat & Equipment

## 1. Overview
Combat in Sigilborne is "Systemic". It is not just animations playing; it is physics-based detection coupled with deep stat calculations.

**GDD References**: B09 (Combat Core), B13 (Weapons), C05 (World Bosses).

---

## 2. The Physics Layer (Body)

### **2.1 Hitbox & Hurtbox**
We use standard Godot `Area2D` nodes for detection, but the logic is decoupled.

*   **Hurtbox**: Attached to the Entity (Player/Enemy). Defines "Where I can be hit".
    *   Layers: `HurtboxLayer`
    *   Data: `BodyPart` (Head, Torso, Limbs).
*   **Hitbox**: Attached to the Weapon/Projectile. Defines "Where I am hitting".
    *   Layers: `HitboxLayer`
    *   Data: `DamageProfileID` (Reference to C# data).

### **2.2 Detection Logic**
When `Hitbox` enters `Hurtbox`:
1.  **Body**: Detects collision via `area_entered` signal.
2.  **Body**: Sends `HitEvent` to the Brain.
    *   `GameManager.Combat.RegisterHit(AttackerID, DefenderID, HitboxData, HurtboxData)`
3.  **Brain**: Calculates the result.
4.  **Brain**: Emits `OnDamageTaken` signal.
5.  **Body**: Spawns blood particles, plays sound, flashes sprite.

---

## 3. The Math Layer (Brain)

### **3.1 Damage Calculator**
The Brain handles the math to ensure cheating/desync is impossible and to support complex formulas.

```csharp
public struct DamageResult
{
    public float FinalDamage;
    public bool IsCrit;
    public bool IsBlocked;
    public DamageType Type; // Physical, Magical, Void
}

public DamageResult Calculate(StatBlock attacker, StatBlock defender, WeaponData weapon)
{
    // 1. Base Damage
    float damage = weapon.BaseDamage + (attacker.Strength * weapon.Scaling);
    
    // 2. Mitigation
    float mitigation = defender.Armor * (1.0f - weapon.Penetration);
    damage -= mitigation;
    
    // 3. Multipliers
    if (IsBackstab(attacker, defender)) damage *= 1.5f;
    
    return new DamageResult { FinalDamage = Math.Max(0, damage) };
}
```

---

## 4. Equipment & Inventory (Brain)

### **4.1 Inventory Data Structure**
Inventory is a pure data structure, not a list of UI nodes.

```csharp
public struct InventoryItem
{
    public string ItemID; // "iron_sword"
    public int Quantity;
    public float Durability;
    public Dictionary<string, float> Metadata; // For enchantments
}

public class InventorySystem
{
    private InventoryItem[] _slots; // Fixed size array
    
    public bool AddItem(string id, int qty) { ... }
    public void RemoveItem(int slotIndex, int qty) { ... }
}
```

### **4.2 Equipment Logic**
When an item is moved to an "Equipment Slot":
1.  **Brain**: Recalculates `PlayerStats` (Weight, Armor, Attack).
2.  **Brain**: Emits `OnEquipmentChanged(Slot, ItemID)`.
3.  **Body**: Updates the `Sprite2D` or `Bone2D` to show the new weapon.

---

## 5. World Boss Mechanics (C05)

### **5.1 Multi-Part Entities**
World Bosses (Titans) are too big for a single Hitbox.
*   **Architecture**: The Boss is one logical Entity in C#, but has multiple `Hurtbox` nodes in Godot.
*   **Limb Health**: The Brain tracks health for each limb separately.
    *   `BossData.Limbs["LeftLeg"].Health`
*   **Severing**: If a limb's health reaches 0, the Brain emits `OnLimbSevered("LeftLeg")`.
    *   **Body**: Detaches the sprite part, spawns gore, changes boss animation set to "Limping".

### **5.2 Titan AI State**
Bosses use a specialized State Machine that accounts for their massive size (e.g., "Turning" takes 5 seconds).
*   **Phase Transitions**: Triggered by Total Health thresholds (100% -> 75% -> 50%).
# TDD 05: AI, Perception & Ecology

## 1. Overview
The AI in Sigilborne is designed to be "Systemic" and "Simulated". NPCs are not just combatants; they are living entities with needs, schedules, and senses.

**GDD References**: B10 (Stealth), B11 (Sensing), B15 (Animals), B18 (Behavior), C05 (Boss AI).

---

## 2. Perception System (Brain)

### **2.1 Spatial Hashing**
To avoid $O(N^2)$ distance checks, we use a Spatial Hash Grid.
*   **Grid Size**: 128x128 pixels (roughly one chunk).
*   **Logic**: Every entity registers its ID in the grid cell it occupies.
*   **Query**: "Get all entities in cells (X,Y) and neighbors."

### **2.2 The Senses**
Each NPC has a `PerceptionComponent` (C#) with:
1.  **Vision**: Cone check (Dot Product + Raycast).
    *   `CanSee(Target) = InRange && InAngle && RaycastClear`
2.  **Hearing**: Circle check.
    *   `CanHear(SoundEvent) = Distance < Sound.Volume * Listener.Sensitivity`
3.  **Chakra Sense (B11)**: Detects active spells through walls.
    *   `CanSense(Spell) = Spell.Intensity > Distance`

### **2.3 Stealth Mechanics (B10)**
Visibility is not binary. It is a float value (0.0 to 1.0).
*   **Factors**: Light Level (from TileMap), Movement Speed, Camouflage.
*   **Detection Meter**: If `Visibility * Time > Threshold`, the NPC enters "Alert" state.

---

## 3. Decision Making: Utility AI (Brain)

We use **Utility AI** (Scoring) instead of simple Finite State Machines (FSM) for complex behavior.

### **3.1 The Scorer**
Every possible action is given a score (0.0 to 1.0) based on the current context.

*   **Action**: `EatFood`
    *   Score = `(Hunger / 100) * DistanceFactor`
*   **Action**: `AttackEnemy`
    *   Score = `(Aggression + EnemyHealthLow) - (MyHealthLow)`
*   **Action**: `Sleep`
    *   Score = `(Fatigue / 100) * IsNightTime`

### **3.2 The Scheduler (B18)**
NPCs have a daily routine.
*   **Morning**: Work (Farm/Guard).
*   **Evening**: Socialize (Tavern).
*   **Night**: Sleep.
*   **Override**: If `Threat > 0`, break schedule and enter Combat Mode.

---

## 4. Ecology Simulation (Brain)

### **4.1 The "Background" Sim**
Animals and NPCs exist even when the player is far away.
*   **Abstraction**: When a chunk is unloaded, entities become "Virtual Agents".
*   **Simulation**: We update Virtual Agents at a very slow tick rate (e.g., once per minute).
    *   `WolfPack.Update()`: Hunt `DeerPack`. If successful, `WolfPopulation++`.

### **4.2 Spawning**
When the player approaches a chunk:
1.  **Query**: Check `EcologyManager` for Virtual Agents in that chunk.
2.  **Instantiate**: Spawn the actual Godot Nodes (`CharacterBody2D`) at the correct positions.
3.  **Sync**: Apply the current stats (Health, Hunger) from the virtual data.

---

## 5. World Boss AI (C05)

### **5.1 The Director**
World Bosses are scripted encounters driven by a "Director" system.
*   **Phase 1**: Introduction. Boss uses basic attacks.
*   **Phase 2**: Escalation. Boss gains new moves, environment changes (Weather).
*   **Phase 3**: Desperation. Boss uses "Ultimate" attacks (C04 Forbidden Arts).

### **5.2 Limb Independence**
Each limb can have its own mini-AI.
*   **Left Hand**: Swipes at players in the left quadrant.
*   **Right Hand**: Smashes players in the right quadrant.
*   **Head**: Casts breath attacks at the furthest player.
# TDD 06: Society & Economy

## 1. Overview
The world of Sigilborne is not static. Factions war, prices fluctuate, and laws are enforced. This chapter details the "Grand Strategy" layer running in the background.

**GDD References**: B16 (Villages), B17 (Factions), B22 (Crime), B23 (Economy), C03 (Contracts).

---

## 2. Faction System (Brain)

### **2.1 The Relationship Graph**
Factions are nodes in a graph; relationships are the edges.
*   **Data**: `FactionRelation { Value: -100 to 100, State: War/Neutral/Alliance }`
*   **Dynamics**:
    *   **Events**: "Clan A raided Clan B" -> `Relation -= 20`.
    *   **Decay**: Relations drift towards 0 (Neutral) over time.

### **2.2 Faction AI**
Each Faction has a "Goal" (e.g., Expansion, Wealth, Religious).
*   **Turn-Based**: The Faction AI runs once per "Game Day".
*   **Actions**:
    *   `DeclareWar(Target)`
    *   `SendCaravan(Destination)`
    *   `BuildOutpost(Location)`

### 2.3 The Simulation Clock
The world does not run at 60 FPS. It runs on "Game Time".
*   **Tick Rate**: 1 Tick = 1 In-Game Minute (approx 1 real second).
*   **Daily Cycle**:
    *   **06:00**: `FactionAI.PlanDay()` (High CPU).
    *   **08:00**: `CaravanSystem.Depart()`.
    *   **12:00**: `MarketSim.UpdatePrices()` (Medium CPU).
    *   **22:00**: `CrimeSystem.DecayHeat()`.
*   **Load Balancing**: We stagger these updates across frames to prevent lag spikes.

### 2.4 Execution Timing (Visual)
To ensure smooth performance, we distribute heavy systems across the daily cycle.

| Time | System | Action | Cost |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **00:00** | `HistoryGen` | Archive daily logs | Low |
| **06:00** | `FactionAI` | Plan strategic moves | **High** |
| **08:00** | `CaravanSys` | Spawn/Depart caravans | Medium |
| **12:00** | `MarketSim` | Recalculate prices | Medium |
| **18:00** | `QuestSys` | Check time-based failures | Low |
| **22:00** | `CrimeSys` | Decay heat/bounties | Low |

*   **World Event Impact**: Major events (e.g., Famine, Collapse) act as global modifiers to these systems.
    *   *Example*: `Famine` event multiplies `MarketSim` food prices by 3.0x and increases `CrimeSys` aggression.

---

## 3. Economy Simulation (Brain)

### **3.1 Market Simulation**
Prices are not fixed. They are local to each Settlement.
*   **Supply & Demand**:
    *   `Price = BasePrice * (Demand / Supply)`
*   **Modifiers**:
    *   **War**: Weapons/Armor price ++.
    *   **Famine**: Food price ++.
    *   **Surplus**: If a player sells 1000 Iron, the price crashes locally.

### **3.2 Trade Routes**
NPC Caravans physically move between settlements (simulated in background).
*   **Flow**: Village A (Iron Mine) -> Caravan -> City B (Smithy).
*   **Interruption**: If the player/bandits destroy the caravan, City B runs out of Iron -> Weapon prices spike.

---

## 4. Crime & Justice (B22)

### **4.1 The Heat System**
Crime is tracked per Faction.
*   **Crimes**: Theft, Assault, Murder, Trespassing.
*   **Witnesses**: A crime is only recorded if a `Witness` (NPC) sees it and reports it.
    *   *Stealth Mechanic*: Kill the witness before they reach a guard -> No Bounty.

### **4.2 Bounty & Punishment**
*   **Bounty**: A gold value on the player's head.
*   **Consequences**:
    *   **Low**: Guards refuse to talk.
    *   **Medium**: Guards attack on sight.
    *   **High**: Faction sends "Hunter Squads" (Elite NPCs) to track the player.

---

## 5. Spirit Contracts (C03)

### **5.1 The Contract Data**
A Contract is a binding agreement between the Player and a Spirit/Entity.
*   **Structure**:
    *   `Conditions`: "Kill 10 Void Beasts", "Do not use Fire Magic".
    *   **Rewards**: "Unlock Mythic Spell X".
    *   **Penalties**: "Lose 50% Max Health".

### **5.2 Enforcement**
The Brain checks contract conditions every Tick.
*   **Violation**: If `Player.HasUsedFireMagic` and `Contract.ForbidsFire`, trigger `Penalty`.
*   **Completion**: If `KillCount >= 10`, trigger `Reward`.
# TDD 07: Progression & Meta-Game

## 1. Overview
Sigilborne is a Roguelite-RPG. Death is not the end; it is a transition. This chapter covers how progress is tracked across runs and how the world evolves.

**GDD References**: B06 (Bloodlines), B20 (Quests), B30 (Legacy), C07 (NG+), C09 (Lore).

---

## 2. Quest System (Brain)

### **2.1 The Quest Graph**
Quests are not linear lists. They are Directed Acyclic Graphs (DAGs).
*   **Nodes**: `QuestStep` (e.g., "Talk to Elder", "Kill 5 Rats").
*   **Edges**: Conditions (e.g., "If Elder is dead -> Fail").
*   **Procedural Quests**: Generated at runtime by the `QuestGenerator`.
    *   Template: `[Action] [Target] at [Location] for [Reward]`.

### **2.2 Quest State**
*   **Active**: Currently tracked.
*   **Completed**: History.
*   **Failed**: History (but may trigger consequences).
### 2.3 Quest Execution Loop
Quests are not passive data; they need to react to the world.
*   **The Quest Ticker**: Runs once per second (1Hz).
*   **Condition Monitoring**:
    *   **Event-Based**: `OnEnemyKilled(ID)` -> Check active quests for "Kill X" steps.
    *   **Time-Based**: `OnTimeChanged(Hour)` -> Check for "Wait until Midnight" steps.
    *   **State-Based**: `OnZoneEntered(ZoneID)` -> Check for "Travel to X" steps.
*   **Failure Conditions**:
    *   If `Quest.FailCondition` is met (e.g., NPC Death), transition state to `Failed` and notify UI.

### **3.1 The Save File**
We use a binary format (Protobuf or MessagePack) for speed and size, as the world state is massive.
*   **Structure**:
    *   `GlobalHeader`: Seed, Playtime, Meta-Currency.
    *   `WorldState`: Compressed Chunk Data (Terrain modifications).
    *   `EntityState`: List of all persistent NPCs (ID, Pos, Stats).
    *   `PlayerState`: Inventory, Stats, Position.

### **3.2 Serialization Strategy**
*   **Chunk-Based**: We only save chunks that have been *modified*.
*   **Delta Compression**: Save the difference between the generated terrain and the current state.

---

## 4. Bloodlines & Legacy (B06, B30)

### **4.1 The Bloodline Tree**
Players do not just create a character; they play a lineage.
*   **Traits**: Genetic perks/flaws passed down.
    *   `EagleEye` (Vision +10%), `Hemophilia` (Bleed Resist -50%).
*   **Inheritance**:
    *   When Character A dies, Character B (Child/Heir) inherits 50% of Gold, some Items, and Traits.

### **4.2 History Generator (B30)**
When a run ends and a new one begins (Time Skip):
1.  **Simulate Years**: The Brain runs a high-speed simulation of the world for `N` years.
2.  **Evolve Factions**: Clans expand/collapse.
3.  **Age NPCs**: Children become adults; adults become elders/die.
4.  **Result**: The world is familiar but changed.

---

## 5. New Game+ & Endless Mode (C07, C08)

### **5.1 NG+ Logic**
*   **World Seed**: Re-rolled or Mutated.
*   **Difficulty Scaling**: `GlobalDifficultyMultiplier` increases.
    *   Enemy HP * 1.5, Damage * 1.5.
*   **New Content**: Unlock "Ascended" enemy variants.

### **5.2 Endless Mode (C08)**
*   **Parallel Worlds**: The player travels between different "World Seeds" via portals.
*   **Scaling**: Difficulty increases infinitely with each jump.
*   **Leaderboard**: Track "Highest Floor Reached".

---

## 6. Lore System (C09)

### **6.1 The Codex**
A database of unlocked knowledge.
*   **Triggers**:
    *   `OnKill(EnemyID)` -> Unlock Enemy Entry.
    *   `OnItemPickup(ItemID)` -> Unlock Item Lore.
    *   `OnEnterZone(ZoneID)` -> Unlock Location History.
*   **UI**: A "Book" interface in the menu.
# TDD 08: World Generation & Streaming

## 1. Overview
Sigilborne features an infinite (or near-infinite) procedural world. This requires a robust pipeline for generating and streaming content without frame drops.

**GDD References**: B25 (Travel), B26 (Dungeons), B31 (Terrain), C08 (Parallel Worlds).

---

## 2. World Streaming (Brain)

### **2.1 Chunk Architecture**
The world is divided into `Chunks` (e.g., 64x64 tiles).
*   **Coordinate System**: `Vector2Int ChunkCoord`.
*   **Active Radius**: The player loads chunks within a radius (e.g., 5 chunks).
*   **Threaded Loading**:
    1.  **Request**: `WorldStreamer` identifies new chunks needed.
    2.  **Generate (Thread)**: C# generates the data (Noise, Biome, Objects).
    3.  **Mesh (Thread)**: C# calculates the TileMap data.
    4.  **Apply (Main Thread)**: Godot `TileMapLayer` is updated in one frame.

### **2.2 Parallel Worlds (C08)**
To support "Dimension Hopping", the `WorldStreamer` must support multiple active `WorldData` instances.
*   **Implementation**: `Dictionary<int, WorldData> Worlds`.
*   **Switching**: When the player enters a portal, we:
    1.  Serialize current chunks.
    2.  Unload all visuals.
    3.  Load chunks from `Worlds[TargetDimensionID]`.

---

## 3. Procedural Generation (Brain)

### **3.1 Terrain Generator**
We use `FastNoiseLite` (C# wrapper) for speed.
*   **Biomes**: Determined by `Temperature` (Noise A) and `Humidity` (Noise B).
    *   High Temp + Low Hum = Desert.
    *   High Temp + High Hum = Jungle.
*   **Heightmap**: Determines Water, Sand, Grass, Mountain.

### **3.2 Dungeon Grammar (B26)**
Dungeons are not noise-based; they are graph-based.
*   **Algorithm**: "Cyclic Dungeon Generation" (or similar).
    1.  **Layout**: Place Rooms (Nodes) and Hallways (Edges).
    2.  **Keys/Locks**: Place a Key in Room A that opens Door in Room B.
    3.  **Theme**: Apply a "Skin" (Ruins, Cave, Temple) to the layout.

---

## 4. Navigation & Pathfinding (Brain)

### **4.1 A* on Grids**
Godot's `NavigationServer2D` is powerful, but for thousands of units, we need a hierarchical approach.
*   **Local Navigation**: Godot `NavigationAgent2D` for obstacle avoidance (RVO).
*   **Global Navigation**: C# A* on the Chunk Grid (Coarse pathfinding).
    *   Path: Chunk A -> Chunk B -> Chunk C.

### **4.2 Dynamic Updates**
When a player builds a wall or a bridge:
1.  **Update Data**: `TerrainData[x,y].IsWalkable = false`.
2.  **Signal**: `OnTerrainChanged(ChunkCoord)`.
3.  **Rebake**: Trigger a local nav-mesh rebake for that chunk (Async).

### 4.3 Navigation Edge Cases
*   **Chunk Transitions**: When an NPC path crosses a chunk boundary, we do not bake a seamless mesh (too expensive).
    *   **Logic**: The path is split into `[Start -> Edge]` and `[Edge -> End]`. The NPC moves to the edge node, then requests a new path in the next chunk.
*   **Dynamic Obstacles**: Player-built structures trigger a "Dirty" flag on the chunk.
    *   **Refresh Rate**: Dirty chunks are rebaked every 2.0 seconds (throttled) to prevent spam.
*   **Global Handoff**:
    *   If `Distance > 2 Chunks`: Use `GlobalPathfinder` (Chunk-to-Chunk A*).
    *   If `Distance <= 2 Chunks`: Use `LocalPathfinder` (Godot NavigationServer).

### 4.4 Future-Proofing: Environmental Hazards
*   **Tile Flags**: If we add Lava or Deep Water, we use `NavigationRegion2D` cost modifiers.
    *   **Lava**: Cost = 100.0 (Avoid unless impossible).
    *   **Water**: Cost = 5.0 (Prefer bridges).
*   **Logic**: The `DungeonGrammar` assigns these flags during generation based on the `Biome` type.

---

## 5. Visual Integration (Body)

### **5.1 TileMapLayers**
We use Godot 4.5's `TileMapLayer` node.
*   **Layer 0**: Ground (Grass, Sand).
*   **Layer 1**: Details (Flowers, Rocks).
*   **Layer 2**: Collision (Walls, Trees).
*   **Layer 3**: Roofs (Fades out when player enters).

### **5.2 Props & Instancing**
Large objects (Trees, Houses) are not Tiles; they are Scenes.
*   **Pooling**: The `WorldStreamer` manages a `NodePool` for trees to avoid `Instantiate()` lag.
# TDD 09: Advanced World Mechanics

## 1. Overview
This chapter covers the "Mythic" interactions that go beyond simple combat or crafting. Rituals, Seals, and World Catastrophes require specialized systems.

**GDD References**: B27 (Seals), B29 (Collapse), C06 (Catastrophes).

---

## 2. Ritual System (Brain)

### **2.1 Pattern Matching**
Rituals are defined by the spatial arrangement of items in the world.
*   **Definition**:
    *   `Center`: "Altar of Void".
    *   `Radius 3`: 4x "Candle (Lit)".
    *   `Radius 5`: 1x "Sacrifice (Goat)".
*   **Detection**:
    *   The `RitualManager` scans for "Ritual Center" objects.
    *   When activated, it performs a spatial query to verify if the required items are present at the correct relative coordinates.

### **2.2 Execution**
If the pattern matches:
1.  **Consume**: Remove the sacrifice/candles.
2.  **Effect**: Spawn Entity / Change Weather / Open Portal.
3.  **Visuals**: Play a "RitualSequence" (Timeline of particles/sounds).

---

## 3. Seals & Locks (B27)

### **3.1 The Seal Component**
A `Seal` is a logical lock on an object (Door, Chest, NPC).
*   **Types**:
    *   `Physical`: Requires a Key Item.
    *   `Magical`: Requires a specific spell to be cast on it.
    *   `Blood`: Requires the player to take damage near it.
    *   `Time`: Opens only at midnight.

### **3.2 Global Seals**
Some seals affect the entire world (e.g., "The Seal of the Sun").
*   **State**: Stored in `WorldState`.
*   **Effect**: While active, `DayNightCycle` is paused. Breaking it resumes time.

---

## 4. The Collapse System (B29, C06)

### **4.1 The Doom Clock**
The world has a finite lifespan.
*   **Metric**: `WorldStability` (Float 100.0 -> 0.0).
*   **Decay**: Decreases daily, and decreases faster when "Forbidden Arts" are used.

### **4.2 Catastrophe Stages**
As Stability drops, global flags are set.
*   **Stage 1 (75%)**: "The Thinning". Magic costs less Mana but more Stability. Sky turns purple.
*   **Stage 2 (50%)**: "The Bleed". Void Beasts spawn naturally in the wild.
*   **Stage 3 (25%)**: "The Collapse". Gravity fluctuates. Tiles randomly turn into "Void Fluid".
*   **Stage 4 (0%)**: "Game Over". The world is deleted (or reset for NG+).

### **4.3 Catastrophe Events (C06)**
Specific large-scale disasters.
*   **The Flood**: `SeaLevel` rises by 1 meter per hour.
    *   **Tech**: The `WaterChunk` generation threshold is adjusted dynamically.
*   **The Eternal Night**: `SunIntensity` set to 0. Temperature drops globally.
# TDD 10: Audio & VFX Pipeline

## 1. Overview
While the Brain handles the logic, the Body must sell the fantasy. This chapter details the "Juice"â€”the audio and visual feedback systems.

**GDD References**: All Systems (Feedback).

---

## 2. Audio Architecture (Body)

### **2.1 AudioManager**
A central singleton wrapper around Godot's `AudioServer`.
*   **Buses**: Master, Music, SFX, UI, Voice, Ambience.
*   **Pooling**: We do not `Instantiate` an AudioStreamPlayer for every gunshot. We use a pool of ~32 players.
    *   `AudioManager.PlayOneShot(Stream, Position, PitchRandom)`

### **2.2 Dynamic Music System**
Music is not a static loop; it reacts to the `GameState`.
*   **Layers**:
    *   `Base`: Ambient drone (Always on).
    *   `Tension`: Percussion (Enemies nearby).
    *   `Action`: Full orchestra (Combat).
*   **Transitions**: We use `Tween` to fade volume of layers based on `CombatIntensity` (calculated by Brain).

### **2.3 Material-Based Footsteps**
1.  **Animation Event**: The `AnimationPlayer` emits a "Footstep" signal.
2.  **Raycast**: We cast a ray down from the foot bone.
3.  **Detection**:
    *   If `TileMap`: Get `CustomData` of the tile (e.g., "Stone", "Grass").
    *   If `Collider`: Get `PhysicsMaterial`.
4.  **Play**: `AudioManager.Play("footstep_" + material)`.

---

## 3. Visual Effects (Body)

### **3.1 Particle Pooling**
Instantiating `GPUParticles2D` causes lag.
*   **System**: `VFXManager` pre-instantiates 50 "BloodSplatter", 20 "FireExplosion", etc.
*   **Usage**:
    *   `VFXManager.Spawn("Blood", Position, Rotation)` -> Teleports an inactive particle system, emits, and schedules sleep.

### **3.2 Screen Shake (Trauma)**
    1.  Plays Sound (Audio).
    2.  Spawns Particles (VFX).
    3.  Shakes Camera (Feedback).
    4.  Flashes Screen (UI).
# TDD 11: Entity & Component Architecture

## 1. Overview
This chapter defines the "Atomic Unit" of the simulation: The Entity.
To support thousands of NPCs (Ecology) and complex interactions (Combat), we cannot rely on Godot Nodes for the simulation data. We need a lightweight, cache-friendly **Entity-Component-System (ECS-lite)** architecture in the Brain.

**GDD References**: All Systems.

---

## 2. The Entity Model (Brain)

### **2.1 Entity ID Structure**
Entities are identified by a unique `EntityID` struct, not a class reference.
*   **Struct**: `readonly struct EntityID { int Index; int Generation; }`
*   **Index**: The slot in the global entity array.
*   **Generation**: A version counter to detect "Use After Free" bugs (accessing an entity that was destroyed and whose slot was reused).

### **2.2 The Entity Registry**
A central `EntityManager` manages the lifecycle.
*   **Storage**: `Entity[] _entities` (Fixed size, e.g., 10,000).
*   **Lookup**: `Dictionary<int, EntityID>` is **NOT** used. Direct array access via `Index` is O(1).
*   **Validation**: `bool IsValid(EntityID id) => _entities[id.Index].Generation == id.Generation;`

---

## 3. Component Architecture

We do not use a full "Pure ECS" (Archetypes/Chunks) like Unity DOTS, as it is overkill for this scale. We use a **Composition over Inheritance** approach with typed data buckets.

### **3.1 Component Storage**
Components are `structs` or `classes` stored in typed arrays/lists within the `EntityManager` or specific Systems.

*   **Pattern**: "SoA" (Structure of Arrays) where possible for hot paths.
    *   `MovementSystem` holds `Vector2[] Positions` and `Vector2[] Velocities`.
*   **Pattern**: "Dictionary" for sparse data.
    *   `InventorySystem` holds `Dictionary<EntityID, InventoryData>`.

### **3.2 Core Components**
Every active entity has:
1.  **TransformComponent**: Position (World Space), Rotation.
2.  **TypeComponent**: Enum (Player, NPC, Animal, Projectile).
3.  **StateComponent**: Flags (IsActive, IsSleeping, IsDead).

---

## 4. Lifecycle Management

### **4.1 Creation (Spawning)**
1.  **Request**: `EntityManager.CreateEntity(DefinitionID)`
2.  **Allocation**: Find free slot in `_entities`. Increment Generation.
3.  **Initialization**: Copy base stats from `DefinitionDatabase`.
4.  **Body Sync**: Emit `OnEntitySpawned(EntityID, Type, Position)`.
    *   **Body**: Instantiates the corresponding Godot Scene.

### **4.2 Destruction (Despawning)**
1.  **Request**: `EntityManager.DestroyEntity(EntityID)`
2.  **Cleanup**: Remove components from all systems.
3.  **Body Sync**: Emit `OnEntityDespawned(EntityID)`.
    *   **Body**: `queue_free()` the Godot Node.
4.  **Recycle**: Mark slot as free.

---

## 5. Virtual vs. Active Agents (Ecology)

To support the "Living World" (B15), entities exist in two states.

### **5.1 Active State (Loaded Chunk)**
*   **Representation**: Full Entity with all Components (Physics, AI, Pathfinding).
*   **Update Rate**: Every Tick (20Hz).
*   **Body**: Has a visual representation (Node2D).

### **5.2 Virtual State (Unloaded Chunk)**
*   **Representation**: "Lightweight" data struct stored in `EcologyManager`.
    *   `struct VirtualAgent { int DefID; Vector2 Pos; float Health; }`
*   **Update Rate**: Slow Tick (e.g., every 10 seconds).
*   **Body**: None.

### **5.3 Transition (Hydration/Dehydration)**
*   **Hydrate**: When player enters chunk -> Convert `VirtualAgent` -> `Entity`.
*   **Dehydrate**: When player leaves chunk -> Convert `Entity` -> `VirtualAgent` -> Destroy `Entity`.

---

## 6. System Iteration
Systems iterate over data, not objects.

```csharp
public class MovementSystem
{
    public void Tick(float dt)
    {
        // Iterate only over entities with Velocity
        foreach (var id in _velocities.Keys)
        {
            var pos = _positions[id];
            var vel = _velocities[id];
            _positions[id] = pos + (vel * dt);
        }
    }
}
```
# TDD 12: Input & Control Flow

## 1. Overview
This chapter defines how raw player input is captured, processed, and routed to the correct system (Movement, Magic, UI). It covers the "Shift-Sliding" mechanic and input prioritization.

**GDD References**: B05 (Hotbar), B25 (Travel).

---

## 2. Input Architecture (Body -> Brain)

### **2.1 The Input Manager (Body)**
Located in `_Body/Scripts/Core/InputManager.gd`.
*   **Responsibility**: Captures hardware events (`_unhandled_input`), normalizes them, and sends them to the Brain.
*   **Normalization**: Converts WASD / Joystick into a `Vector2` (Clamped length 1.0).

### **2.2 The Input Frame (Interop)**
We send a snapshot of input to the Brain every tick.

```csharp
public struct PlayerInputFrame
{
    public Vector2 MoveVector; // X,Y (-1 to 1)
    public Vector2 LookVector; // Mouse position or Stick
    public bool IsSprintHeld;
    public bool IsShiftHeld; // For "Sliding"
    public bool[] HotbarKeys; // 1-0
    public bool InteractPressed;
}
```

---

## 3. Movement Logic (Brain)

### **3.1 Standard Movement**
*   **Input**: `MoveVector`.
*   **Logic**: `Velocity = MoveVector * Speed`.
*   **Friction**: High friction when input stops (Snappy movement).

### **3.2 Shift-Sliding (The Mechanic)**
"Holding shift allows player to release movement input, but the character keeps walking in the last specified input."

*   **State**: `LastMoveVector` (Vector2).
*   **Logic**:
    ```csharp
    if (Input.IsShiftHeld)
    {
        if (Input.MoveVector != Vector2.Zero)
        {
            // Override direction while holding shift
            LastMoveVector = Input.MoveVector;
        }
        // Keep moving in the locked direction
        TargetVelocity = LastMoveVector * Speed;
    }
    else
    {
        // Normal movement
        LastMoveVector = Input.MoveVector;
        TargetVelocity = Input.MoveVector * Speed;
    }
    ```

---

## 4. Action Routing & Priority

The `PlayerController` (Brain) decides which system gets the input.

### **4.1 Priority Stack**
1.  **UI**: If a Menu is open, it consumes all input.
2.  **Interaction**: If `InteractPressed` and `Target` in range -> Trigger Interaction.
3.  **Magic**: If `HotbarKey` pressed -> Route to `MagicSystem` (InputBuffer).
4.  **Combat**: If `AttackPressed` -> Route to `CombatSystem`.
5.  **Movement**: If no other blocking action -> Apply Velocity.

### **4.2 Action Queue**
To prevent button mashing issues, we use a short buffer (0.2s) for actions.
*   **Scenario**: Player presses "Attack" while in "Recovery" animation.
*   **Result**: The attack is queued and executes immediately when Recovery ends.

---

## 5. Hotbar Routing (B05)

### **5.1 Key Mapping**
*   **Keys 1-9**: Mapped to `GlyphType` (Fire, Water, etc.).
*   **Key 0**: Mapped to `Ultimate` or `Consumable`.

### **5.2 Logic**
When Key `N` is pressed:
1.  **Check**: Is the Hotbar Slot `N` unlocked?
2.  **Get**: The `GlyphID` assigned to that slot.
3.  **Send**: `MagicSystem.InputBuffer.Push(GlyphID, Time.time)`.
4.  **Feedback**: Emit `OnHotbarPressed(N)` for UI animation.
# TDD 13: Job System & Concurrency

## 1. Overview
Sigilborne requires updating thousands of agents (Ecology), generating terrain (WorldGen), and calculating complex paths (AI). Doing this on the Main Thread will cause stutter. We need a robust **Job System**.

**GDD References**: B15 (Ecology), B25 (World Gen), B18 (NPC Schedules).

---

## 2. The Job Architecture (Brain)

### **2.1 The Job Manager**
A central singleton that manages a pool of worker threads.
*   **Worker Pool**: `N` threads (where N = Logical Cores - 1).
*   **Queues**:
    *   `HighPriority`: Pathfinding, Combat Logic (Immediate).
    *   `LowPriority`: Ecology Sim, World Gen (Background).

### **2.2 The Job Struct**
Jobs are `structs` to avoid GC allocation.
```csharp
public interface IJob
{
    void Execute();
}

public struct EcologyUpdateJob : IJob
{
    public int StartIndex;
    public int EndIndex;
    public NativeArray<VirtualAgent> Agents; // Thread-safe array wrapper
    
    public void Execute() { ... }
}
```

---

## 3. Thread Safety Strategy

### **3.1 The "No-Node" Rule**
**CRITICAL**: Jobs NEVER access Godot Nodes (`Node`, `Sprite2D`). They only operate on C# data (POCOs/Structs).

### **3.2 Command Buffers**
Jobs cannot modify the main `EntityManager` directly (Race Conditions).
*   **Solution**: Jobs write to a `CommandBuffer`.
    *   `CommandBuffer.Add(new SpawnEntityCommand(...))`
    *   `CommandBuffer.Add(new DestroyEntityCommand(...))`
*   **Sync Point**: At the start of the next Main Thread Tick, the `GameManager` plays back the Command Buffer to apply changes.

### **3.3 Double Buffering (State)**
For systems like Ecology where we read *and* write state:
*   **Read**: `State[Current]` (ReadOnly).
*   **Write**: `State[Next]`.
*   **Swap**: At end of frame, swap indices.

---

## 4. Specific Implementations

### **4.1 Ecology Simulation (B15)**
*   **Task**: Update hunger/movement for 5,000 virtual animals.
*   **Job**: `EcologyJob`.
*   **Slicing**: Split the array into chunks of 500. Schedule 10 jobs.
*   **Frequency**: Run once every 60 frames (1 second).

### **4.2 Pathfinding (A*)**
*   **Task**: NPC needs a path from A to B.
*   **Job**: `PathfindingJob`.
*   **Input**: `GridSnapshot` (Copy of the grid state).
*   **Output**: `List<Vector2> Path`.
*   **Callback**: When job completes, invoke `NPC.OnPathFound(path)`.

### **4.3 World Generation (B31)**
*   **Task**: Generate noise and mesh data for a new chunk.
*   **Job**: `TerrainGenJob`.
*   **Priority**: Low.
*   **Output**: `ChunkData` struct.
*   **Main Thread**: Applies `ChunkData` to `TileMapLayer`.

---

## 5. C# Implementation Details

We use `System.Threading.Tasks` and `ConcurrentQueue<T>`.

```csharp
public class JobSystem
{
    private ConcurrentQueue<IJob> _queue = new();
    
    public void Schedule(IJob job)
    {
        Task.Run(() => 
        {
            job.Execute();
            // Handle completion on main thread if needed
        });
    }
}
```
*Note: For maximum performance, we may implement a custom `NativeArray` equivalent using `Unsafe` code to avoid pinning/marshaling overhead.*
# TDD 14: World Persistence & Streaming

## 1. Overview
This chapter defines the "Contract" for how the world is saved, loaded, and streamed. It bridges the gap between the **Job System** (TDD 13) and **Progression** (TDD 07).

**GDD References**: B25 (Travel), B30 (Legacy).

---

## 2. Chunk Lifecycle (Brain)

### **2.1 The Chunk State Machine**
Each chunk exists in one of three states:
1.  **Unloaded**: Does not exist in memory. Data is on disk (or ungenerated).
2.  **Virtual (Cached)**: Loaded in memory as data (`ChunkData`), but no Godot Nodes.
    *   *Used for*: Ecology simulation, distant pathfinding.
3.  **Active (Visual)**: Fully instantiated with Godot Nodes (`TileMapLayer`, `StaticBody2D`).

### **2.2 Streaming Logic**
*   **Trigger**: Player moves across a Chunk Boundary.
*   **Action**:
    *   **Front**: Load/Generate new chunks -> `Virtual` -> `Active`.
    *   **Back**: `Active` -> `Virtual` -> `Unloaded` (Save to disk).

---

## 3. Persistence Architecture

### **3.1 The "Diff" Strategy**
We do not save the entire chunk (which is mostly static procedural noise). We only save **Deltas**.
*   **ChunkData**:
    *   `Seed`: 12345
    *   `Modifications`: List of changes.
        *   `{ Index: 402, TileID: "Dirt" }` (Player dug a hole).
        *   `{ Index: 55, Object: "Chest_Open" }` (Player opened a chest).

### **3.2 Serialization Format**
*   **File**: `world_region_X_Y.save` (Region = 32x32 chunks).
*   **Format**: Binary (Protobuf).
    *   `Header`: Version, Timestamp.
    *   `Chunks`: Array of compressed Deltas.

### 3.3 Save Versioning & Migration
To prevent corruption when the game updates:
*   **Header**: Contains `SaveVersion` (int).
*   **Migration Logic**:
    ```csharp
    if (header.Version < CURRENT_VERSION)
    {
        Migrator.Run(data, header.Version, CURRENT_VERSION);
    }
    ```
*   **Safety**: If a migration fails, we load the backup file (`.bak`).

---

## 4. Virtual Agent Sync (The Hard Part)

How do we persist NPCs that move between loaded and unloaded chunks?

### **4.1 The Handover**
When a chunk is unloaded, all **Active Entities** in it must be converted to **Virtual Agents**.
1.  **Serialize**: `EntityID 101` -> `VirtualAgent { ID: 101, Pos: (10, 5), HP: 50 }`.
2.  **Store**: Add to `EcologyManager.VirtualAgents`.
3.  **Destroy**: `EntityManager.DestroyEntity(101)`.

### **4.2 The Restoration**
When a chunk is loaded:
1.  **Query**: `EcologyManager.GetAgentsInChunk(ChunkCoord)`.
2.  **Spawn**: For each Virtual Agent, call `EntityManager.CreateEntity()`.
3.  **Restore**: Apply the saved stats (HP, Inventory).

---

## 5. Concurrency Safety
Saving happens on a background thread (Job System).
*   **Snapshot**: Before saving, we take a **Deep Copy** of the Chunk Data on the Main Thread.
*   **Write**: The worker thread writes the Snapshot to disk.
*   **Locking**: We use a `ReaderWriterLockSlim` on the Region File to prevent reading while writing.
# TDD 15: Glyph Generation (Prototype B)

## 1. Overview
In Sigilborne, "Fire" is not always the "Triangle" glyph. The meaning of glyphs is procedurally randomized per world seed. This chapter details the **Glyph Generation System**.

**GDD References**: B01 (Glyphs), B04 (Mastery).

---

## 2. The Glyph Database (Brain)

### **2.1 Concepts vs. Symbols**
We separate the *Mechanical Effect* from the *Visual Symbol*.
*   **Concepts**: `Fire`, `Water`, `Void`, `Push`, `Pull`, `Self`.
*   **Symbols**: `Triangle`, `Circle`, `Square`, `Spiral`, `Dot`.

### **2.2 Generation Logic**
At the start of a new run (New World):
1.  **Shuffle**: Create a list of all available Symbols.
2.  **Assign**: Map Symbols to Concepts using the World Seed.
    *   *Run A*: Triangle = Fire.
    *   *Run B*: Triangle = Void.
3.  **Store**: Save this mapping in `WorldData.GlyphMap`.

---

## 3. The Discovery System

Players do not know the mapping at the start. They must learn it.

### **3.1 Knowledge State**
*   **Hidden**: Player sees the symbol "???" or a blurred rune.
*   **Seen**: Player has seen the rune cast by an NPC, but doesn't know the meaning.
*   **Known**: Player has successfully cast a spell using this rune or read a scroll.

### **3.2 Experimentation**
*   **Input**: Player presses "Triangle" + "Circle".
*   **Result**:
    *   If `Triangle=Fire` and `Circle=Push` -> Casts "Fireball".
    *   **Feedback**: The game reveals "Triangle is Fire!" (UI Notification).
    *   **Failure**: If the combo is invalid, the spell fizzles, and the player takes `Stability` damage.

---

## 4. Subtypes & Modifiers

### **4.1 Procedural Nuance**
Glyphs have "Subtypes" that are also randomized.
*   **Fire Glyph Variants**:
    *   *Variant A*: High Heat, Low Range (Blue Flame).
    *   *Variant B*: Low Heat, High Explosion (Red Flame).
*   **Generation**:
    *   The generator assigns specific float modifiers to each Variant ID.

### **4.2 Teachers & Scrolls**
*   **Scroll**: An item that, when used, sets the `KnowledgeState` of a specific Glyph to `Known`.
*   **Teacher**: An NPC that demonstrates a combo. The player's `InputBuffer` records the sequence, allowing them to "replay" it to learn.
# TDD 16: Scene Composition & Body Standards

## 1. Overview
To prevent "Scene Spaghetti", we enforce strict standards on how Godot Scenes (`.tscn`) are composed. The Body is a **View**, not a Controller.

**GDD References**: System_Language_Architecture.

---

## 2. Node Hierarchy Standards

### **2.1 The Entity Root**
Every active entity scene MUST follow this structure:

```text
CharacterBody2D (Root)      <- Named "EntityRoot". Has "EntityView.gd".
â”œâ”€â”€ Visuals (Node2D)        <- Rotates/Flips.
â”‚   â”œâ”€â”€ Sprite (Sprite2D)
â”‚   â””â”€â”€ VFX (Node2D)        <- Attachment point for particles.
â”œâ”€â”€ Collision (CollisionShape2D)
â”œâ”€â”€ Audio (Node2D)          <- Attachment point for sounds.
â””â”€â”€ UI (Control)            <- Health bars, Name tags.
```

### **2.2 Script Responsibilities**
*   **EntityView.gd**: The ONLY script that talks to the Brain.
    *   *Allowed*: Interpolating position, playing animations, emitting input signals.
    *   *Forbidden*: Calculating damage, storing inventory, decision making.

---

## 3. Naming Conventions

### **3.1 Files**
*   **Scenes**: PascalCase. `PlayerCharacter.tscn`, `IronSword.tscn`.
*   **Scripts**: snake_case. `entity_view.gd`, `camera_controller.gd`.
*   **Assets**: snake_case. `icon_fire_ball.png`, `sfx_footstep_grass.wav`.

### **3.2 Nodes**
*   **Functional**: PascalCase. `Sprite`, `CollisionShape`, `AnimationPlayer`.
*   **Unique**: `MainCamera`, `WorldEnvironment`.

---

## 4. Scene Interfaces

### **4.1 The "Setup" Function**
Every Entity Scene must have a `setup(id: int)` function.
```gdscript
# entity_view.gd
var entity_id: int

func setup(id: int) -> void:
    entity_id = id
    # Connect to Brain signals
    GameEvents.connect("entity_moved", _on_entity_moved)
```

### **4.2 Visual Interpolation**
The Body runs at a higher framerate than the Brain.
*   **Logic**:
    ```gdscript
    func _process(delta: float) -> void:
        var target_pos = Brain.GetPosition(entity_id)
        global_position = global_position.lerp(target_pos, delta * SMOOTHING_SPEED)
    ```

---

## 5. Animation Event Protocol
To sync the "Puppet" (Body) with the "Logic" (Brain), we use a strict event standard.

### **5.1 The Signal Standard**
Animations MUST NOT call functions directly. They emit signals via the `EntityView`.
*   **Format**: `anim_event(type: String, payload: Dictionary)`

### **5.2 Standard Event Types**
*   **"hit_frame"**: The exact moment a weapon connects.
    *   *Payload*: `{ "hitbox_id": "sword_slash_01" }`
    *   *Brain Action*: Activates the Hitbox logic for 1 frame.
*   **"footstep"**: Frame where foot touches ground.
    *   *Payload*: `{ "bone": "left_foot" }`
    *   *Brain Action*: None (Handled by Body Audio).
*   **"cast_release"**: Moment a spell projectile spawns.
    *   *Payload*: `{ "socket": "right_hand" }`
    *   *Brain Action*: Spawns the Projectile Entity.

### 5.3 Future-Proofing: IK & Physics Bones
*   **IK Handles**: If using Inverse Kinematics (e.g., for feet placement), use `Marker2D` nodes named `IK_Target_L` and `IK_Target_R`.
*   **Physical Bones**: For ragdolls, ensure `PhysicalBone2D` nodes are on the **Physics Layer** but disabled until death to prevent collision jitter.


# TDD 17: Physics & Collision Interop

## 1. Overview
Sigilborne uses a **Hybrid Physics Architecture**.
*   **Brain (C#)**: Authoritative for Velocity, Position, and Logic.
*   **Body (Godot)**: Authoritative for Collision Detection and Separation (Slide).

**GDD References**: B09 (Combat), B25 (Travel).

---

## 2. The Movement Pipeline

### **2.1 The "Brain-Driven" Frame**
1.  **Input**: Brain receives `MoveVector`.
2.  **Velocity**: Brain calculates `TargetVelocity` (Speed, Friction, External Forces).
3.  **Integration**: `ProposedPosition = CurrentPosition + (Velocity * Delta)`.
4.  **Sync**: Brain sends `ProposedPosition` + `Velocity` to Body.

### **2.2 The "Body-Resolved" Frame**
1.  **Receive**: Body gets `ProposedPosition`.
2.  **MoveAndSlide**: Body calls `CharacterBody2D.move_and_slide()` using the Brain's velocity.
3.  **Correction**: Godot's physics engine resolves collisions (walls, slopes).
4.  **Feedback**: Body sends the *actual* `FinalPosition` back to the Brain at the end of the frame.

### **2.3 Reconciliation**
*   **Brain**: Overwrites its internal `CurrentPosition` with the Body's `FinalPosition`.
*   **Why?**: Implementing a full physics engine in C# is unnecessary. We trust Godot to handle "don't walk through walls", but we tell it *where* we want to go.

---

## 3. Interactions & Pushes

### **3.1 Knockback**
*   **Source**: Brain (Combat System).
*   **Action**: `Velocity += KnockbackVector`.
*   **Result**: The next `MoveAndSlide` on the Body will naturally handle the slide/wall collision.

### **3.2 Entity-vs-Entity Push**
*   **Layer**: Entities are on a "Soft Collision" layer.
*   **Logic**: `CharacterBody2D` handles this automatically via `motion_mode`.
*   **Brain Awareness**: The Brain does *not* need to know about micro-collisions between NPCs, only their final positions.

---

## 4. Physics Layers (Standard)

| Layer Name | Bit | Contents |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **World** | 1 | Walls, Terrain, Trees |
| **Player** | 2 | The Player Hurtbox |
| **Enemy** | 3 | Enemy Hurtboxes |
| **Projectile** | 4 | Magic, Arrows |
| **Interaction** | 5 | Chests, NPCs (Talk) |
| **Hitbox** | 6 | Weapon Swings |
# TDD 18: Status Effects & Conditions

## 1. Overview
Status Effects (Buffs/Debuffs) are the glue between Combat, Magic, and Biology. They require a standardized lifecycle to prevent bugs like "Infinite Burn" or "Stacking Speed Boosts".

**GDD References**: B12 (Injury), B09 (Combat), C04 (Void Sickness).

---

## 2. The Effect Data Structure (Brain)

### **2.1 Definition vs. Instance**
*   **EffectDefinition**: Static data.
    *   `ID`: "burn_t1"
    *   `Type`: DoT (Damage over Time)
    *   `MaxStacks`: 5
    *   `Duration`: 10.0s
    *   `TickRate`: 1.0s
*   **ActiveEffect**: Runtime instance on an Entity.
    *   `DefinitionID`: "burn_t1"
    *   `Stacks`: 3
    *   `TimeRemaining`: 4.5s
    *   `SourceID`: EntityID of the caster (for kill credit).

---

## 3. Lifecycle Management

### **3.1 Application**
When `ApplyEffect(Target, EffectID)` is called:
1.  **Check**: Does the target already have this effect?
2.  **If No**: Create new `ActiveEffect`.
3.  **If Yes**:
    *   **Refresh**: Reset `TimeRemaining` to Max.
    *   **Stack**: Increment `Stacks` (up to Max).

### **3.2 The Tick Loop**
The `StatusEffectSystem` iterates over all active effects.
*   **OnTick**:
    *   If `Type == DoT`: `Target.Health -= Damage * Stacks`.
    *   If `Type == StatMod`: `Target.Stats.Speed *= 0.5` (Recalculated every frame).
*   **Cleanup**: If `TimeRemaining <= 0`, remove the effect.

---

## 4. Specific Mechanics

### **4.1 Void Sickness (C04)**
*   **Type**: Permanent (until cured).
*   **Logic**:
    *   Stack 1-20: Visual Glitches.
    *   Stack 21-50: `MaxHealth` reduced by 20%.
    *   Stack 51-99: Randomly invert controls.
    *   Stack 100: Instant Death (Spawn Void Beast).

### **4.2 Bleed (B12)**
*   **Type**: Movement-based DoT.
*   **Logic**:
    *   Damage is multiplied by `Target.Velocity.Length()`.
    *   *Encourages players to stand still to stop bleeding.*

---

## 5. Visual Hooks (Body)

The Brain emits signals when effects change.
*   **Signal**: `OnEffectApplied(EntityID, EffectID)`
    *   **Body**: Spawns a particle loop (Fire) attached to the entity.
*   **Signal**: `OnEffectRemoved(EntityID, EffectID)`
    *   **Body**: Detaches/Destroys the particle loop.
# TDD 19: Appendix & Reference

## 1. Glossary

| Term | Definition |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Brain** | The C# simulation layer. Handles logic, data, and state. Runs on a fixed tick (20Hz). |
| **Body** | The GDScript visual layer. Handles rendering, audio, and input capture. Runs on frames (60Hz+). |
| **EntityID** | A `struct { Index, Generation }` used to uniquely identify an entity in the Brain. |
| **Virtual Agent** | A lightweight data representation of an NPC in an unloaded chunk. |
| **Chunk** | A 32x32 tile section of the world. Can be Active, Virtual, or Unloaded. |
| **Tick** | A single update step of the simulation. Deterministic and fixed-step. |
| **Frame** | A single render loop of the Godot engine. Variable timing. |
| **Interop** | The communication bridge between C# and GDScript (Signals, Calls, Marshaling). |
| **Residue** | A magical byproduct that accumulates in chunks, causing mutations and void sickness. |
| **Glyph** | A symbol used in spellcasting. Its mechanical meaning is randomized per world seed. |
| **Job System** | A multithreaded worker pool for heavy tasks (Ecology, Pathfinding). |
| **EventBus** | A central hub for decoupling systems via C# Actions/Delegates. |

---

## 2. System Call Graph (Execution Order)

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Main Loop (GameManager.cs)"
        Input[1. Input Processing] --> Jobs[2. Job Completion]
        Jobs --> Sim[3. Simulation Tick (20Hz)]
        Sim --> Physics[4. Physics Reconciliation]
        Physics --> Interop[5. State Sync]
    end

    subgraph "Simulation Tick"
        Time[Time System] --> Events[Event Bus Flush]
        Events --> Bio[BioSim Update]
        Bio --> AI[AI Decision]
        AI --> Combat[Combat Resolution]
        Combat --> Magic[Magic System]
    end

    subgraph "Body (Godot Frame)"
        Interop --> Interpolate[Visual Interpolation]
        Interpolate --> VFX[VFX & Audio]
        VFX --> Render[Render Frame]
    end
```

---

## 3. Networking Future-Proofing

While Sigilborne is single-player, the **Brain/Body separation** makes it "Network Ready".

### **3.1 Architecture Suitability**
*   **Server-Authoritative**: The "Brain" is effectively a local server. The "Body" is a local client.
*   **State Sync**: We already separate `State` (Brain) from `View` (Body). Sending `State` over a socket instead of a memory bridge is a manageable refactor.

### **3.2 Required Changes for Co-op**
1.  **Input**: Instead of reading `InputManager` directly, the Brain would process a `Queue<InputFrame>` received from the Network.
2.  **EntityIDs**: Would need a "NetworkID" mapping to ensure clients agree on which entity is which.
3.  **Determinism**: The Brain is mostly deterministic, but `System.Random` would need to be replaced with a seeded `NetworkRandom` to ensure clients simulate identical results.

---

## Target Stack
Godot 4.5
